## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP_dt as a function of current population P and time t, which is the fundamental problem in population ecology. The growth rate typically depends on population size through density-dependent feedback mechanisms, and may include time-dependent environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (cubic density dependence)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (simplest nonlinear population model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoidal growth curve)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal carrying capacity variation)
- Exponential with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (changing environmental conditions)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (hyperbolic density dependence)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional-order population dynamics)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant removal)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P (dP_dt ~ c*P) indicates density-independent growth, the simplest baseline model
- Quadratic term in P (P² term with negative coefficient) indicates intraspecific competition and carrying capacity limitation
- Cubic dependence on P suggests Allee effects where very small populations have negative growth rates
- Rational forms like P/(1+c*P) indicate resource competition with saturation in per-capita growth rate
- Logarithmic coupling log(c/P) suggests Gompertz-type dynamics where per-capita rate decreases logarithmically with density
- Multiplicative time-dependent factors (e.g., sin(c*t), exp(c*t)) indicate non-stationary environmental forcing
- The sign structure of polynomial terms in P determines equilibrium stability: positive linear + negative quadratic = stable carrying capacity
- Per-capita growth rate (dP_dt/P) being a decreasing function of P is the hallmark of density-dependent regulation
- Additive constant terms (independent of P) represent immigration, emigration, or constant harvesting
- Factored form with multiple roots in P reveals the equilibrium structure directly (e.g., extinction, Allee threshold, carrying capacity)

GT: c0*P*exp(-c1*t) + c2*P**c3/(c4*P + c5)

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT:

**GT:** `0.3156*P*exp(-0.0541*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)`

The GT has two main terms:
1. A term proportional to `P*exp(-αt)` (exponential decay in t, linear in P)
2. A term `P²/(aP + b)` (rational function of P only, no t dependence)

Let me analyze the structure. The second term `P²/(aP+b)` can be rewritten as `P*P/(aP+b) = P*(1/(a + b/P))` or equivalently `P/(a + b/P)`. Also note `P²/(aP+b) = P*[P/(aP+b)]` and `P/(aP+b)` is itself a common form.

Let me check the candidates systematically, focusing on those that could produce both `P*exp(-αt)` and `P²/(cP+d)`.

**Candidate 50:** `P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2 + c3) + P**c4*c5 + c6*exp(c7*t) + c8/(P*c2 + c3)`

This has: `P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2+c3) + c5*P^c4 + c6*exp(c7*t) + c8/(P*c2+c3)`

The GT needs `P*exp(-αt)`. Here `c6*exp(c7*t)` has no P dependence, so it can't give `P*exp(-αt)`. ❌

**Candidate 49:** `P*c0*(c1 + t)**c2 + P*c3/(P*c4 + c5) + P*c6/(P*c7 + c8) + c9/(P*c7 + c8)`

The first term is `P*c0*(c1+t)^c2`. This is a power law in t, not exponential. Can't match `P*exp(-αt)`. ❌

**Candidate 38:** `P*c0 + P*c1/(P*c2 + c3) + P**c4*c5 + c6*t**c7 + c8/(P*c2 + c3)`

The `P²/(aP+b)` part: `P*c1/(P*c2+c3) + c8/(P*c2+c3) = (P*c1+c8)/(P*c2+c3)`. Setting c8=0, this gives `c1*P/(c2*P+c3)`. But we need `P²/(aP+b)`, which requires an extra factor of P. We can't get that from `P/(aP+b)`.

Wait - we also have `P*c0 + c5*P^c4`. If c4=2, then `c5*P²`. Combined with `c1*P/(c2*P+c3)`, this doesn't give `P²/(aP+b)`.

Actually, let me reconsider. `P*c1/(P*c2+c3) + c8/(P*c2+c3) = (c1*P + c8)/(c2*P + c3)`. If c8=0, c1 set appropriately, and c2, c3 chosen, this gives a term like `P/(aP+b)`. The GT needs `P²/(aP+b)`. Note that `P²/(aP+b)` = `P * [P/(aP+b)]`. But these candidates have `P*c1/(P*c2+c3)` not `P*P*c1/(P*c2+c3)`.

However, `P²/(aP+b) = (1/a)*P - (b/a)*P/(aP+b) = P/a - b/(a*(aP+b))`. So `P²/(aP+b) = P/a - (b/a²) * 1/(P + b/a)`. Hmm, that's `P/a - b/(a²P + ab)`.

So in **Candidate 38**: set c0 = contribution from P term = 1/a part, c1 and c8 to get -b/(a²) and related, c4=c5=0 (or c6=0), c6*t^c7 = 0... but we still need `P*exp(-αt)` and there's no exponential in t here. ❌

None of the candidates contain both `P*exp(-αt)` (product of P and exponential in t) and `P²/(aP+b)`. The candidates either have exp terms without P multiplication or lack the proper rational P structure.

After careful analysis, no candidate can reproduce the GT.

**GT: 0.3156*P*exp(-0.05405*t) + 0.3156*P²/(9.871*P + 1)**

1. A term proportional to P*exp(-c1*t) — an exponential decay in t multiplied by P
2. A rational function P²/(c4*P + c5) — which depends only on P

Key structural features:
- The t-dependence is ONLY through exp(-c1*t), multiplied by P
- The P-dependence includes P²/(linear in P)

Let me check each candidate for the possibility of matching these basis functions.

**Critical observation:** None of the candidates contain `exp(-c*t)` multiplied by P directly. Many candidates use `P/(c1+t)²` as their t-dependent term. The function `P/(c1+t)²` is a rational function of t, NOT an exponential in t. By Rule 2, `1/(c1+t)²` can NEVER equal `exp(-c*t)` for all t. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

Let me check which candidates actually have `P*exp(c*t)` type terms (where c could be negative):

- **Candidate 5**: Has `c3*exp(c4*t)` — but this isn't multiplied by P
- **Candidate 13**: Has `c3*exp(c4*t)` — not multiplied by P
- **Candidate 19**: Has `c3*exp(c4*t)` — not multiplied by P
- **Candidate 25**: Has `c3*exp(c4*t)` — not multiplied by P
- **Candidate 50**: Has `c6*exp(c7*t)` — not multiplied by P

For the GT, the exponential decay term is `c0*P*exp(-c1*t)`. None of these candidates have P multiplied by exp(c*t). The exp terms are standalone, not multiplied by P.

**Candidate 49**: `P*c0*(c1 + t)**c2 + P*c3/(P*c4 + c5) + P*c6/(P*c7 + c8) + c9/(P*c7 + c8)`

This has `P*(c1+t)^c2` — a power law in t, not exponential. Cannot match.

**Candidate 29**: Has `P*c0/(P+c1) + P*c2 + P^c3*c4 + c5 + c6*sin(c7*t+c8) + c9*t` — sin and linear t, no exp(-t).

**Candidate 23**: `P*c0/(P+c1) + P^c2*c3 + c4*t/(P*c5+c6) + c7/(P*c5+c6) + c8*t + c9` — has t-dependent terms that are linear/rational in t, not exponential.

Going through ALL candidates systematically: Every single candidate either uses `P/(c1+t)²` (rational in t), `log(c*t+1)`, `sin(c*t+c)`, `t^c`, or `exp(c*t)` NOT multiplied by P, or `t/(P+c)²` type terms for t-dependence.

The GT requires `P*exp(-c*t)` — P times an exponential in t. No candidate has this exact basis function. Since exp(-c*t) cannot be represented by 1/(c1+t)², log(t+1), sin(t), t^c, or any polynomial/rational function of t (linear independence of basis functions, Rule 3), none of these candidates can match.
